   119	## GC / hot-set
   120	
   121	```rust
   122	/// Opaque view-handle id assigned by the actor (monotonically increasing u64).
   123	#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug, Eq, PartialEq, Hash)]
   124	pub struct ClaimerId(pub u64);
   125	
   126	/// Budget for one `gc_step()` call.
   127	#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug)]
   128	pub struct GcBudget {
   129	    pub max_events_per_step: usize,
   130	    pub max_duration_ms: u32,
   131	}
   132	
   133	/// Report produced by `gc_step()`.
   134	#[derive(Clone, Debug, Default)]
   135	pub struct GcReport {
   136	    pub expired_reaped: usize,
   137	    pub lru_evicted: usize,
   138	    pub tombstones_purged: usize,
   139	    pub duration_ms: u32,
   140	}
   141	```
   142	
   143	## Export
   144	
   145	```rust
   146	#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug)]
   147	pub enum DumpFormat { Jsonl, Cbor }
   148	
   149	#[derive(Clone, Debug, Default)]
   150	pub struct DumpStats {
   151	    pub events: u64,
   152	    pub tombstones: u64,
   153	    pub watermarks: u64,
   154	    pub domain_rows: u64,
   155	    pub bytes_written: u64,
   156	}
   157	```
   158	
   159	## Errors
   160	
   161	```rust
   162	#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)]
   163	pub enum StoreError {
   164	    #[error("backend i/o: {0}")] Io(String),
   165	    #[error("backend corruption: {0}")] Corrupt(String),
   166	    #[error("encoding: {0}")] Encoding(String),
   167	    #[error("schema too new: {namespace} on-disk={on_disk} expected={expected}")]
   168	    SchemaTooNew { namespace: String, on_disk: u32, expected: u32 },
   169	    #[error("schema migration failed: {namespace} v{from}->v{to}: {reason}")]
   170	    MigrationFailed { namespace: String, from: u32, to: u32, reason: String },
   171	    #[error("unknown namespace: {0}")] UnknownNamespace(String),
   172	    /// Returned by `claim()` when the per-view or global pinned ceiling is exceeded.
   173	    /// The claim is rejected; no pin is written. The caller must release some
   174	    /// existing claim or reduce the requested set before retrying.
   175	    /// Maps to D8 (reactivity contract): a working-set overflow must be surfaced
   176	    /// as a typed rejection, never silently tolerated (see ADR-0001..0004).
   177	    #[error("claim ceiling exceeded: claimer={claimer:?} requested={requested} ceiling={ceiling}")]
   178	    OverPinned { claimer: ClaimerId, requested: usize, ceiling: usize },
   179	}
   180	```
   181	
   182	No `StoreError` ever crosses FFI (D6). The actor maps every variant to a typed `Effect` or a graceful degraded state. See [`../trait.md`](../trait.md) §5 for the full mapping.

 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	# LMDB sub-design: test plan
     2	
     3	> Part of [`docs/design/lmdb-schema.md`](../lmdb-schema.md). Maps every insert invariant in `docs/product-spec/subsystems.md` §7.1 to a concrete test in `crates/nmp-testing/tests/`. Each test exists for both `MemEventStore` (always) and `LmdbEventStore` (under `#[cfg(feature = "lmdb-backend")]`).
     4	
     5	## 1. Test harness shape
     6	
     7	```rust
     8	// crates/nmp-testing/src/store_harness.rs
     9	pub struct StoreHarness {
    10	    pub store: Box<dyn EventStore>,
    11	    pub tmp: tempfile::TempDir,
    12	    pub keys: nostr::Keys,
    13	}
    14	
    15	impl StoreHarness {
    16	    pub fn mem() -> Self { /* MemEventStore */ }
    17	    pub fn lmdb() -> Self { /* LmdbEventStore in tmp dir */ }
    18	
    19	    pub fn insert(&self, builder: EventBuilder, source: &str) -> InsertOutcome { /* ... */ }
    20	    pub fn assert_present(&self, id: &EventId);
    21	    pub fn assert_tombstoned(&self, id: &EventId);
    22	    pub fn restart(&mut self);   // close + reopen the store; LMDB only
    23	}
    24	
    25	// Tests use a macro to run against both backends.
    26	macro_rules! for_each_backend {
    27	    ($name:ident, $body:expr) => {
    28	        #[test] fn $name() { let mut h = StoreHarness::mem(); $body(&mut h); }
    29	        #[cfg(feature = "lmdb-backend")]
    30	        #[test] fn paste::paste!([<$name _lmdb>])() {
    31	            let mut h = StoreHarness::lmdb(); $body(&mut h);
    32	        }
    33	    };
    34	}
    35	```
    36	
    37	The harness lives in `crates/nmp-testing/src/` so per-test files are short and declarative.
    38	
    39	## 2. Invariant → test mapping
    40	
    41	Every row of the §7.1 table:
    42	
    43	### 2.1 Insert API single path (§7.1 row "Insert API")
    44	
    45	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_insert_path.rs`
    46	
    47	```rust
    48	for_each_backend!(insert_returns_insert_outcome, |h: &mut StoreHarness| {
    49	    let event = h.signed(EventBuilder::text_note("hello", &[]));
    50	    let outcome = h.store.insert(event.clone(), &"wss://t/".into(), 0).unwrap();
    51	    assert!(matches!(outcome, InsertOutcome::Inserted { .. }));
    52	    assert!(h.store.get_by_id(&event.id.to_bytes()).unwrap().is_some());
    53	});
    54	```
    55	
    56	Plus a runtime-instrumented test enforcing that `insert()` is the only path that writes to the primary `events` sub-db. The test uses a `WriteCounting<S>` newtype that wraps any `EventStore` and intercepts every write; at teardown it asserts that all writes to the primary sub-db originated from `insert()` call frames (verified via a `AtomicBool` flag set on entry to `insert` and checked inside the write interceptor).
    57	
    58	```rust
    59	// crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_insert_path.rs
    60	struct WriteCounting<S: EventStore> {
    61	    inner: S,
    62	    in_insert: Arc<AtomicBool>,
    63	    illegal_primary_writes: Arc<AtomicUsize>,
    64	}
    65	
    66	// ...wraps every EventStore method; every put() to the primary sub-db checks
    67	// in_insert; increments illegal_primary_writes if false.
    68	for_each_backend!(only_insert_writes_primary, |h: &mut StoreHarness| {
    69	    let wc = WriteCounting::wrap(h.take_store());
    70	    // Exercise every non-insert method that could conceivably write.
    71	    let _ = wc.delete_by_filter(DeleteFilter::ByIdList(vec![]));
    72	    let _ = wc.gc_step(GcBudget { max_events_per_step: 0, max_duration_ms: 0 });
    73	    assert_eq!(wc.illegal_primary_writes.load(Ordering::SeqCst), 0);
    74	});
    75	```
    76	
    77	### 2.2 Signature verification (§7.1 row "Signature/delegation validity")
    78	
    79	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_invalid_sig.rs`
    80	
    81	Builds an event, mutates the signature, inserts. Expects `InsertOutcome::Rejected { reason: RejectReason::BadSignature }` and no row in primary, secondaries, provenance, or tombstones. Also tests a malformed NIP-26 delegation tag (rejects with `BadDelegation`).
    82	
    83	### 2.3 Duplicate id → provenance merge (§7.1 row "Duplicate id")
    84	
    85	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_provenance_merge.rs`
    86	
    87	```rust
    88	for_each_backend!(duplicate_merges_provenance_keeps_earliest, |h| {
    89	    let ev = h.signed(EventBuilder::text_note("x", &[]));
    90	    let o1 = h.store.insert(ev.clone(), &"wss://a/".into(), 1000).unwrap();
    91	    let o2 = h.store.insert(ev.clone(), &"wss://b/".into(), 2000).unwrap();
    92	    assert!(matches!(o1, InsertOutcome::Inserted { .. }));
    93	    assert!(matches!(o2, InsertOutcome::Duplicate { sources_after: 2, .. }));
    94	    let p = h.store.provenance_for(&ev.id.to_bytes()).unwrap();
    95	    assert_eq!(p.len(), 2);
    96	    let primary = p.iter().find(|e| e.primary).unwrap();
    97	    assert_eq!(primary.relay_url, "wss://a/");
    98	    assert_eq!(primary.first_seen_ms, 1000); // earliest preserved
    99	});
   100	```
   101	
   102	### 2.4 Replaceable supersession (§7.1 row "Replaceable kinds")
   103	
   104	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_replaceable.rs`
   105	
   106	Inserts two kind:0 from same pubkey, second with later `created_at`. Asserts: `get_by_id(first_id)` returns None; `scan_by_author_kind(pk, &[0], None, None, 10)` returns one row; the row's id is the second. Tie-break test: two kind:0 with same `created_at` — keep the lexicographically smaller id.
   107	
   108	### 2.5 Parameterized replaceable (§7.1 row "Parameterized replaceable")
   109	
   110	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_param_replaceable.rs`
   111	
   112	Insert two kind:30023 with same `(pubkey, d=foo)`, second newer; assert only the second is returned by `get_param_replaceable(pk, 30023, b"foo")`. Insert a third with same kind+pubkey but `d=bar` — assert both `foo` and `bar` are independently retrievable. Assert that a kind:30024 with `d=foo` (different kind) does not collide with the kind:30023.
   113	
   114	### 2.6 Kind:5 self-delete + tombstone persistence (§7.1 row "Kind 5")
   115	
   116	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_kind5_tombstone.rs`
   117	
   118	- Insert kind:1 by Alice.
   119	- Insert kind:5 by Alice referencing the kind:1 via `e` tag.
   120	- Assert kind:1 gone from primary; tombstone row exists with `target_id == kind1.id`, `origin == Kind5`.
   121	- Insert the same kind:1 again — assert `InsertOutcome::Tombstoned`, no primary row created.
   122	- Restart store; repeat the re-insertion — assert tombstone persists across restart.
   123	
   124	### 2.7 Foreign kind:5 ignored (§7.1 row "Kind 5" — foreign clause)
   125	
   126	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_kind5_foreign.rs`
   127	
   128	- Insert kind:1 by Alice.
   129	- Insert kind:5 by Bob referencing Alice's kind:1.
   130	- Assert: kind:1 is still present in primary (Bob can't delete Alice's event); the kind:5 event itself is stored (so other clients can see it); no tombstone row was written.
   131	
   132	### 2.7a Kind:5 `a`-tag delete arriving before the target event
   133	
   134	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_kind5_addr_tombstone.rs`
   135	
   136	Tests the `tombstones_addr` sub-db path (see [`keys.md`](keys.md) §4.2):
   137	
   138	```rust
   139	for_each_backend!(a_tag_delete_before_event_suppresses_reinsert, |h: &mut StoreHarness| {
   140	    // Build a kind:5 that references a kind:30023 by address (not yet in store).
   141	    let d_tag = "my-article";
   142	    let addr = format!("30023:{}:{}", h.keys.public_key(), d_tag);
   143	    let kind5 = h.signed(EventBuilder::new(Kind::from(5), "", vec![
   144	        Tag::parse(vec!["a", &addr]).unwrap(),
   145	    ]));
   146	    let outcome5 = h.store.insert(kind5.clone(), &"wss://t/".into(), 0).unwrap();
   147	    // The kind:5 itself should be stored (for other clients to render).
   148	    assert!(matches!(outcome5, InsertOutcome::Inserted { .. } | InsertOutcome::Duplicate { .. }));
   149	
   150	    // Now insert the target parameterized replaceable event.
   151	    let article = h.signed(EventBuilder::new(Kind::from(30023), "hello", vec![
   152	        Tag::parse(vec!["d", d_tag]).unwrap(),
   153	    ]));
   154	    let article_id = article.id.to_bytes();
   155	    let outcome_article = h.store.insert(article, &"wss://t/".into(), 0).unwrap();
   156	    // Must be suppressed because the address tombstone matches.
   157	    assert!(
   158	        matches!(outcome_article, InsertOutcome::Tombstoned { origin: TombstoneOrigin::Kind5, .. }),
   159	        "expected Tombstoned, got {outcome_article:?}"
   160	    );
   161	    assert!(h.store.get_by_id(&article_id).unwrap().is_none(), "article must not be stored");
   162	
   163	    // Confirm that a subsequent re-insertion of the same article is also suppressed
   164	    // (the address tombstone should have promoted an event-id tombstone for the specific id).
   165	    let article2 = h.signed_with_id(article_id, EventBuilder::new(Kind::from(30023), "hello", vec![
   166	        Tag::parse(vec!["d", d_tag]).unwrap(),
   167	    ]));
   168	    let outcome2 = h.store.insert(article2, &"wss://t/".into(), 0).unwrap();
   169	    assert!(matches!(outcome2, InsertOutcome::Tombstoned { .. }));
   170	});
   171	```
   172	
   173	Restart variant: `h.restart()` between the kind:5 insert and the article insert — assert the address tombstone survives the restart.
   174	
   175	### 2.8 NIP-40 expiration scheduling (§7.1 row "NIP-40 expiration")
   176	
   177	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_nip40_expiration.rs`
   178	
   179	- Insert kind:1 with `expiration` tag at `now + 1 second`.
   180	- Assert `scan_expiring_before(now + 5, 10)` returns the event.
   181	- Call `gc_step(GcBudget { max_events_per_step: 10, max_duration_ms: 100 })` at `now + 2`.
   182	- Assert primary row gone; tombstone written with `origin == NIP40Expiry`.
   183	- Insert same event again — assert `InsertOutcome::Tombstoned`.
   184	- Insert an event with `expiration` already in the past — assert `InsertOutcome::Rejected { reason: ExpiredOnArrival }`.
   185	- Restart store; insert new event with `expiration` at `now + 1`; assert the reaper picks it up after restart (the `idx_expires` cursor scan is the source of truth — no separate timer needs to survive restart).
   186	
   187	### 2.9 Watermarks (§7.1 "Sync watermarks")
   188	
   189	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_watermarks.rs`
   190	
   191	- Write a watermark; read it back; assert equal.
   192	- Restart store; read again; assert preserved.
   193	- Test `coverage()`: row with `synced_up_to = now - 60s` → `Coverage::CompleteAsOf` (under default 300s staleness); row with `synced_up_to = now - 600s` → `Coverage::PartialUpTo`; missing row → `Coverage::Unknown`.
   194	- `list_watermarks_for_relay("wss://a/")` returns only rows for that relay.
   195	- Concurrent writes to the same key (simulated): last-writer-wins, no row corruption.
   196	
   197	### 2.10 Claims + GC (§7.1 "GC")
   198	
   199	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_gc_claims.rs`
   200	
   201	- Insert 100 events; all in hot LRU (under default 10k ceiling).
   202	- Claim 10 of them under `ClaimerId(1)`.
   203	- Configure `target_hot_size = 50`; insert another 50 events; call `gc_step`.
   204	- Assert: 10 claimed events still present in hot (`store.get_by_id` is a fast in-memory hit — measurable via a counter exposed for the test); 40 unclaimed events evicted from LRU but still readable from disk.
   205	- Release `ClaimerId(1)`; insert another 20 events; call `gc_step`.
   206	- Assert: previously claimed events now subject to LRU eviction.
   207	
   208	### 2.11 Dump round-trip (master doc §10)
   209	
   210	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_dump_roundtrip.rs`
   211	
   212	- Build a populated store: 1000 events, 50 tombstones, 100 watermarks, 200 domain rows across 3 namespaces.
   213	- `dump(&mut buf1, DumpFormat::Jsonl)`.
   214	- Open a fresh store; replay every line; `dump(&mut buf2, ...)`.
   215	- Assert `buf1 == buf2` byte-for-byte (sort by stable key first — the dump iterates sub-dbs in a deterministic order documented in the dump module).
   216	
   217	### 2.12 Domain migration success + failure (master doc §6)
   218	
   219	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_domain_migration.rs`
   220	
   221	- Register `TestModuleV1` with `SCHEMA_VERSION = 1` and no migrations; open store; assert `_meta.test_module.schema_version == 1`.
   222	- Close store; register `TestModuleV2` with `SCHEMA_VERSION = 2` and one migration v1→v2 that writes one key; open store; assert migration ran and key exists.
   223	- Close; register `TestModuleV3` with `SCHEMA_VERSION = 3` and a deliberately failing migration v2→v3; open store; assert `Effect::DomainSchemaTooNew { namespace: "test_module" }` (under degraded-mode rules) and `_meta` still at v2.
   224	- Close; remove the failing migration; reopen — assert successful catch-up to v3 (idempotent retry).
   225	
   226	### 2.12a Migration atomicity / crash-recovery (watermarks.md §4.2)
   227	
   228	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_domain_migration.rs` (extended section)
   229	
   230	Tests the single-`RwTxn` atomicity invariant for migration steps: verifies that a simulated crash (i.e., aborting the write transaction mid-migration) leaves the `_meta` version unchanged and the store in a retryable state.
   231	
   232	```rust
   233	#[cfg(feature = "lmdb-backend")]
   234	#[test]
   235	fn migration_crash_leaves_version_unchanged() {
   236	    // Use a FailingMigration that panics after writing data but before commit.
   237	    // We catch the unwind and re-open the store.
   238	    let dir = tempfile::tempdir().unwrap();
   239	    let result = std::panic::catch_unwind(|| {
   240	        let store = LmdbEventStore::open(dir.path()).unwrap();
   241	        let migrations = vec![DomainMigration {
   242	            from_version: 0,
   243	            to_version: 1,
   244	            apply: Box::new(|tx| {
   245	                tx.put(b"key", b"value")?;
   246	                panic!("simulated crash after data write, before commit");
   247	            }),
   248	        }];
   249	        let _ = store.run_migrations("test_ns", 1, &migrations);
   250	    });
   251	    assert!(result.is_err(), "expected panic");
   252	
   253	    // Re-open: version must still be 0 (data write was not committed).
   254	    let store2 = LmdbEventStore::open(dir.path()).unwrap();
   255	    let version = store2.read_meta_schema_version_raw("test_ns").unwrap().unwrap_or(0);
   256	    assert_eq!(version, 0, "version must not be bumped after a crashed migration");
   257	    // The data write must also be absent (rolled back with the transaction).
   258	    let handle = store2.domain_open("test_ns").unwrap();
   259	    assert!(handle.get(b"key").unwrap().is_none());
   260	}
   261	```
   262	
   263	### 2.13 Domain isolation (`kernel-substrate.md` §8)
   264	
   265	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_domain_isolation.rs`
   266	
   267	- Open `DomainHandle` for module A; write key `K`.
   268	- Open `DomainHandle` for module B; read key `K` — assert returns `None`.
   269	- Module B's `scan_prefix(b"")` returns only module B's rows.
   270	
   271	### 2.14 Cold-start performance (master doc §12)
   272	
   273	Scenario in `crates/nmp-testing/bin/firehose-bench/src/scenarios/cold_start.rs` (already exists in M1; extended here):
   274	
   275	- Pre-populate an LMDB store with a representative session (~20k events: 10k kind:1, 8k kind:0, 2k kind:3 / 10002).
   276	- Tar + ship the file with the test fixture.
   277	- Measure: open store, register modules, run the bootstrap sequence that the actor runs on app launch, until the first `AppUpdate::FullState` is emitted with non-empty timeline.
   278	- Gate: ≤ 1.5 s on iPhone 12 hardware; ≤ 800 ms on iPhone 16 Pro simulator.
   279	
   280	### 2.15 Working-set memory (ADR-0003)
   281	
   282	Scenario in `crates/nmp-testing/bin/reactivity-bench` — extended with a new `--scenario working_set_lmdb` mode:
   283	
   284	- Insert 1M synthetic events into the store.
   285	- Open 100 view subscriptions covering 10k events.
   286	- Run for 60 seconds with light churn (insert 10 events / sec).
   287	- Sample RSS every 5 seconds via `/proc/self/status` on Linux / `mach_task_basic_info` on iOS.
   288	- Gate: max RSS ≤ 100 MB over the run.
   289	
   290	### 2.16 Restart preserves replaceable semantics (`plan.md` §M3 exit gate)
   291	
   292	File: `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_replaceable_restart.rs`
   293	
   294	- Write kind:0 v1; assert present.
   295	- Write kind:0 v2 (newer); assert v1 gone, v2 present.
   296	- Restart store; assert v2 still present, v1 still gone.
   297	- Write kind:0 v0 (older than v2); assert no change (`InsertOutcome::Superseded`).
   298	
   299	## 3. Property tests
   300	
   301	In `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_props.rs` using `proptest`:
   302	
   303	- **Insert is total under random valid events.** Generate a vec of valid signed events, insert in any order, assert the store's `get_by_id` agrees with the model (a `HashMap` reference impl).
   304	- **Replaceable convergence.** For any sequence of replaceable inserts for the same `(pubkey, kind, [d])` key, the final stored event is the (max created_at, min id) winner regardless of insertion order.
   305	- **Provenance commutativity.** For any two relay sources `r1, r2` and identical event, the post-state of provenance is identical to inserting `r2` first then `r1`.
   306	- **`nmp dump` is a fixed point.** Round-trip equality after N random operations.
   307	
   308	## 4. Cross-test invariants (asserted in a `teardown` hook for every test)
   309	
   310	Every test ends with `harness.assert_invariants()`:
   311	
   312	1. Every event in the primary store has a `provenance` row with ≥ 1 entry.
   313	2. Every secondary index entry's `event_id` resolves to an existing primary row.
   314	3. Every tombstone's `target_id` does **not** exist in the primary store.
   315	4. The `_meta._kernel.schema_version` is at the latest version the binary knows.
   316	5. The hot LRU contains only events that exist in the primary store.
   317	
   318	Violation of any invariant fails the test with a precise diff of which sub-db is out of sync.
   319	
   320	## 5. CI integration
   321	
   322	`cargo test --workspace --features lmdb-backend` becomes part of the pre-merge gate from M3 onward (`plan.md` §6 will be updated). The criterion benches in `crates/nmp-testing/benches/store_*.rs` run nightly with regression checks against the previous week's median (>5% regression on any p99 fails the nightly).

/bin/zsh -lc 'nl -ba docs/decisions/0011-lmdb-env-sharing.md' in /Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform
 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	# ADR 0011: NMP owns the LMDB environment and injects it into nostr-lmdb
     2	
     3	**Date:** 2026-05-18
     4	**Status:** accepted
     5	**Resolves:** `docs/design/lmdb-schema.md` §13 open question 1
     6	**Depends on:** ADR-0009 (kernel boundary), ADR-0003 (working-set memory)
     7	
     8	## Context
     9	
    10	The M3 persistence layer wraps `nostr-lmdb` (the upstream Rust crate) behind NMP's own `EventStore` trait. The implementation holds both (a) a `NostrLMDB` for canonical event storage and (b) NMP-owned secondary LMDB sub-databases (provenance, watermarks, claims, domain rows, tombstones).
    11	
    12	The core atomicity requirement is: **every `insert()` call must commit event + provenance + all NMP secondary index entries in a single LMDB write transaction.** This is mandatory because:
    13	
    14	- A crash between the primary write and the secondary writes would leave the index in a state inconsistent with the primary store — the next `scan_by_author_kind` could return stale or missing results.
    15	- A crash between the migration data writes and the `_meta` version write would re-run an already-committed migration step, potentially corrupting migrated data.
    16	
    17	Per doctrine D6: "errors never cross FFI as exceptions." The corollary is that the *store itself* must never silently produce an incorrect answer because of partial writes. Any scenario where two separate `lmdb::Environment` handles could each commit independently would violate this — we would have no way to roll back one side when the other fails.
    18	
    19	**Why this matters (D6):** if the store returns wrong data because of a partial write, that wrong data eventually reaches FFI as an `AppUpdate`. There is no way to signal "this snapshot is partially corrupt" through a `Result<T, StoreError>` once the data is already in the `AppUpdate` struct. The only safe design is to prevent partial writes at the store layer.
    20	
    21	## Decision
    22	
    23	**NMP owns the `lmdb::Environment` and injects it into `nostr-lmdb`.**
    24	
    25	Concretely:
    26	
    27	1. `LmdbEventStore::open(path)` calls `lmdb::Environment::open(path, ...)` and receives the sole `Environment` handle.
    28	2. This `Environment` is passed to `NostrLMDB` via a new constructor `NostrLMDB::with_env(env: Arc<lmdb::Environment>) -> Self` (an upstream PR to `nostr-lmdb`).
    29	3. Both `nostr-lmdb`'s sub-databases and NMP's sub-databases are opened under this single `Environment`.
    30	4. `insert()` opens one `lmdb::RwTxn`, calls `nostr_lmdb.save_event_in_txn(txn, &event)` plus NMP's secondary writes, then commits once. Either all writes land or none do.
    31	5. Migration steps open one `RwTxn` per step and commit the data writes and the `_meta` version bump together (see `lmdb/watermarks.md` §4.2).
    32	
    33	## How it works
    34	
    35	### Upstream PR
    36	
    37	The upstream PR to `nostr-lmdb` adds:
    38	
    39	```rust
    40	impl NostrLMDB {
    41	    /// Construct with a caller-owned Environment. The caller is responsible for
    42	    /// keeping the Environment alive as long as this NostrLMDB is alive.
    43	    pub fn with_env(env: Arc<lmdb::Environment>, opts: NostrLMDBOptions) -> Result<Self, Error>;
    44	
    45	    /// Insert an event inside an existing write transaction. The caller commits.
    46	    pub fn save_event_in_txn<'txn>(
    47	        &self,
    48	        txn: &mut lmdb::RwTxn<'txn>,
    49	        event: &nostr::Event,
    50	    ) -> Result<SaveEventStatus, Error>;
    51	}
    52	```
    53	
    54	The PR is straightforward: the existing `NostrLMDB` already opens one `Environment` internally; the change is to accept an externally-owned `Arc<Environment>` instead and expose the txn-scoped write primitive.
    55	
    56	### Interim fallback
    57	
    58	If the upstream PR is not merged within the M3 implementation window, we use a pinned fork of `nostr-lmdb` at the commit we need (adding a `[patch.crates-io]` entry in the workspace `Cargo.toml`). The fork carries only the two additions above; no other changes. The fork reference is replaced with the upstream version once the PR lands.
    59	
    60	### Two-phase-write fallback (if environment sharing is impossible)
    61	
    62	If the upstream crate architecture fundamentally prevents sharing the `Environment` (e.g., because it calls `Environment::open` with exclusive flags), the fallback is:
    63	
    64	1. Two separate `Environment` handles: one for `nostr-lmdb`'s sub-dbs, one for NMP's sub-dbs.
    65	2. `insert()` writes to `nostr-lmdb` first (primary + upstream indexes), then to NMP's sub-dbs in a second transaction.
    66	3. On crash recovery at startup, a consistency check compares the two environments' primary event sets against NMP's secondary indexes and replays any NMP writes that didn't land (a WAL-style forward-recovery scan limited to events inserted in the last write window, identified by the `_wal_pending` sub-db).
    67	
    68	This fallback is significantly more complex and has a measurable write-amplification cost. It is not the preferred design and should only be used if the upstream PR path is closed. The check `StoreHealth::consistency_status` (exposed to the diagnostics bridge per ADR-0007) surfaces any out-of-sync state detected at startup so it is always visible to developers.
    69	
    70	## Consequences
    71	
    72	**Positive:**
    73	- Single-commit atomicity for all `insert()` writes. No half-state visible to any reader.
    74	- Simpler recovery: LMDB's built-in crash-recovery (WAL + mmap) is sufficient; no NMP-side recovery logic needed.
    75	- Migration steps are atomic by construction (§4.2 of `lmdb/watermarks.md`).
    76	
    77	**Negative:**
    78	- Requires an upstream PR to `nostr-lmdb`. If the PR is rejected and the crate owner doesn't expose an environment-injection constructor, we must fork. The fork is a maintenance surface.
    79	- NMP becomes the LMDB environment owner, which means it is responsible for tuning `mapsize`, `max_dbs`, and `max_readers`. These were previously handled by `nostr-lmdb` internally. The defaults used by `nostr-lmdb` are well-chosen for Nostr workloads; NMP adopts them as its starting point and adjusts only when benchmarks show a regression.
    80	
    81	## Alternatives considered
    82	
    83	**A. Let `nostr-lmdb` own the environment; use a two-phase write with WAL-recovery.** Described above as the fallback. Rejected as the primary design because of the added complexity, the recovery-window ambiguity, and the write-amplification cost.
    84	
    85	**B. Replace `nostr-lmdb` with a hand-rolled LMDB layer.** Rejected in the master doc §1 (see "Rejected alternatives"). Reinvents 2 000+ LOC of battle-tested NIP-09 / replaceable event logic at high bug risk. Not justified.
    86	
    87	**C. Use SQLite (or another store) that supports multi-table transactions natively.** SQLite supports cross-table ACID transactions without environment sharing issues. Rejected because (a) the iOS-disk-WAL fsync cost at our 10k-event hot working set is higher than LMDB's mmap model, (b) `nostr-lmdb` gives us NIP-77 negentropy integration we would have to re-implement, (c) SQLite is held in reserve for the web port (M15). Re-evaluate if the upstream PR path closes and the fork proves too expensive to maintain.

docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:92:All secondaries are maintained inside the same `RwTxn` as the primary write — atomicity is achieved by LMDB transactionality, not by post-hoc reconciliation. This requires NMP and `nostr-lmdb` to share a single `lmdb::Environment`; the decision is in ADR-0011 (`docs/decisions/0011-lmdb-env-sharing.md`).
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:114:See [`lmdb/watermarks.md`](lmdb/watermarks.md) §4. A `DomainModule` (per `kernel-substrate.md` §2) declares `const NAMESPACE: &'static str` and `const SCHEMA_VERSION: u32` plus `fn migrations() -> Vec<DomainMigration>`. The store assigns one LMDB sub-database per `(namespace, "data")`, plus one per `(namespace, index_name)` for each declared index. A `_meta` sub-database tracks `(namespace, current_version)`.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:116:The current `ModuleRegistry` (`crates/nmp-core/src/substrate/mod.rs:41`) discards the concrete `M: DomainModule` type after `register_domain::<M>()` returns — only the `ModuleDescriptor` is retained. The store cannot get from a namespace string back to `M::SCHEMA_VERSION` or `M::migrations()` at runtime. M3 adds a `DomainFactories { schema_version: fn() -> u32, migrations: fn() -> Vec<DomainMigration>, indexes: fn() -> Vec<DomainIndex> }` struct attached per descriptor, populated by capturing the `M::*` consts and fns in `fn`-pointer closures at register time. This matches the existing `key_fn: fn(&[u8]) -> Option<Vec<u8>>` pattern in `DomainIndex` (`crates/nmp-core/src/substrate/domain.rs:18`) — no `Box<dyn DomainModule>` and no new trait object-safety constraints on `DomainModule`. The change is additive to the substrate module surface. See [`lmdb/watermarks.md`](lmdb/watermarks.md) §4.1 for the registry-side code shape.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:221:1. **`nostr-lmdb` LMDB environment sharing.** ~~Can we open the same `lmdb::Environment` for both `NostrLMDB`'s sub-databases and our own NMP sub-databases?~~ **Resolved by ADR-0011** (`docs/decisions/0011-lmdb-env-sharing.md`): NMP owns the `lmdb::Environment` and injects it into `nostr-lmdb` via an upstream PR (or an interim fork). This gives atomic cross-sub-db transactions for free. See ADR-0011 for the fallback plan if the upstream PR is rejected.

docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:35:            Coverage::CompleteAsOf(row.synced_up_to),

docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:148:            store.run_migration_step(namespace, step)?;
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:152:            return Err(StoreError::MigrationFailed { /* missing step */ });
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:162:**Atomicity invariant:** each `run_migration_step` opens a single `RwTxn` that covers **both** the migration data writes (`step.apply(&mut migration_tx)`) **and** the `_meta` version bump (`write_meta_schema_version(namespace, step.to_version)`). Both writes commit together or neither does. This means a process crash between the data write and the version bump is impossible — if the commit never happened, the version stays at `current` and the migration is retried cleanly on the next startup.
docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:188:- `LogicalInterestStatus.cache_coverage` resolves from `coverage()` (§1.1 above) for the relevant `(filter_hash, relay_url)` pair.
docs/decisions/0011-lmdb-env-sharing.md:5:**Resolves:** `docs/design/lmdb-schema.md` §13 open question 1
docs/decisions/0011-lmdb-env-sharing.md:14:- A crash between the primary write and the secondary writes would leave the index in a state inconsistent with the primary store — the next `scan_by_author_kind` could return stale or missing results.
docs/decisions/0011-lmdb-env-sharing.md:17:Per doctrine D6: "errors never cross FFI as exceptions." The corollary is that the *store itself* must never silently produce an incorrect answer because of partial writes. Any scenario where two separate `lmdb::Environment` handles could each commit independently would violate this — we would have no way to roll back one side when the other fails.
docs/decisions/0011-lmdb-env-sharing.md:19:**Why this matters (D6):** if the store returns wrong data because of a partial write, that wrong data eventually reaches FFI as an `AppUpdate`. There is no way to signal "this snapshot is partially corrupt" through a `Result<T, StoreError>` once the data is already in the `AppUpdate` struct. The only safe design is to prevent partial writes at the store layer.

docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:23:    fn scan_by_author_kind<'a>(
docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:44:    fn scan_by_kind_dtag<'a>(
docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:71:    fn scan_by_kind_time<'a>(

docs/design/lmdb/gc.md:130:**Ceiling defaults** (see `StoreError::OverPinned` in [`trait/types.md`](trait/types.md)):
docs/design/lmdb/gc.md:131:- `max_claim_per_view`: 1 000 events per claimer. A view that tries to pin more returns `OverPinned`; the actor surfaces this as `Effect::ViewOverPinned` and releases the claim.
docs/design/lmdb/gc.md:132:- `max_pinned_total`: 20 000 events globally. Prevents many moderate-sized views from collectively overwhelming the working set (D8 / ADR-0003 gate).

docs/design/lmdb/keys.md:110:### 4.2 Address tombstones (`tombstones_addr` sub-db)
docs/design/lmdb/keys.md:116:On insert of any parameterized replaceable (kinds 30000–39999), the insert pre-check also queries `tombstones_addr.get(pubkey ‖ kind ‖ dtag)`. A hit suppresses the insert and writes an event-id tombstone for the incoming event's id (so future re-insertions of the same id are also caught by the fast `tombstones` lookup). The `InsertOutcome::Tombstoned` returned to the caller has `kind5_event_id = row.kind5_event_id` and `origin = Kind5`.
docs/design/lmdb/keys.md:126:### 5.1 `idx_watermark_relay` (relay-first secondary)
docs/design/lmdb/keys.md:130:Written in the same `RwTxn` as every `write_watermark` call. Enables `list_watermarks_for_relay(relay)` in O(matching rows) by prefix-scanning on `relay_url_bytes`. Without this secondary, the scan would be O(all watermarks) because the primary key is `filter_hash`-first.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:67:- **Reads:** `get_by_id`, `scan_by_author_kind`, `get_param_replaceable`, `scan_by_kind_dtag`, `scan_by_etag`, `scan_by_ptag`, `scan_by_kind_time`, `scan_expiring_before`. All `scan_*` methods return a streaming `EventIter` so the planner pages without materialising. Cache-coverage queries via `coverage(WatermarkKey)` return a `Coverage` enum (`CompleteAsOf`, `PartialUpTo`, `Unknown`) used by the M2 planner.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:69:- **Watermarks / sync:** `read_watermark`, `write_watermark`, `list_watermarks_for_relay`.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:70:- **GC:** `claim(ClaimerId, &[EventId])`, `release(ClaimerId)`, `hot_set_hint(&[EventId])`, `gc_step(GcBudget) -> GcReport`.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:75:**Error semantics.** All methods return `Result<T, StoreError>`. Per doctrine D3, store errors do **not** cross FFI — the actor maps every variant to either (a) a typed `Effect` (e.g. `StoreCorrupt`, surfaces via diagnostics + toast), (b) a `tracing::warn!` log + degraded state, or (c) a panic at startup if the LMDB environment refuses to open. The trait itself uses `Result` since it is internal to the actor process.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:82:- Secondary `idx_author_kind`: `pubkey[32] || kind_be[4] || created_at_desc_be[8] || event_id[32]` → empty. NMP-owned. `created_at_desc_be = (u64::MAX - created_at).to_be_bytes()` for newest-first forward scans.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:83:- Secondary `idx_kind_dtag`: `kind_be[4] || pubkey[32] || dtag_len_be[2] || dtag_bytes` → `event_id[32]`. NMP-owned. Parameterized replaceable address lookup. The `pubkey` field comes before `d-tag` bytes so all entries for a `(kind, pubkey)` pair are contiguous for `scan_by_kind_dtag`.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:84:- Secondary `idx_etag_time`, `idx_ptag_time`: `tag_value[32] || created_at_desc_be[8] || event_id[32]` → `kind_be[4]`. NMP-owned. Value holds kind so reaction views can filter without a primary fetch.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:85:- Secondary `idx_kind_time`: `kind_be[4] || created_at_desc_be[8] || event_id[32]` → empty.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:87:- `tombstones`: `target_id[32]` → CBOR `TombstoneRow { kind5_event_id: Option<[u8;32]>, origin: TombstoneOrigin, deleter_pubkey: Option<[u8;32]>, deleted_at, sources: Vec<RelayUrl> }`.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:88:- `tombstones_addr`: `pubkey[32] || kind_be[4] || dtag_len_be[2] || dtag_bytes` → CBOR `TombstoneRow`. For kind:5 `a`-tag deletes arriving before the target event exists (see [`lmdb/keys.md`](lmdb/keys.md) §4.2).
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:90:All integer fields in keys are big-endian so LMDB's byte-wise comparator matches numeric order. `created_at_desc_be = (u64::MAX - created_at).to_be_bytes()` produces newest-first forward scans without `MDB_LAST + MDB_PREV`.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:123:4. If greater, refuse to start (downgrade not supported); surface as `Effect::DomainSchemaTooNew { namespace }`.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:139:`hot_resident` lives in a `lru::LruCache<EventId, Arc<Event>>` capped at the configured hot ceiling (default 10,000) plus a bounded pinned overlay holding events with non-zero claim count. The pinned overlay has two ceilings: per-view (`max_claim_per_view`, default 1 000) and global (`max_pinned_total`, default 20 000). `claim()` returns `StoreError::OverPinned` if either ceiling would be breached; see [`lmdb/gc.md`](lmdb/gc.md) §2 for enforcement details. `cold` lives only on disk; lookup pays one LMDB `get` (memory-mapped — typically already in OS page cache for recently-evicted items).
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:152:  - For `e` tags: if the target event exists in the store and was authored by the deleter, delete the primary + all secondaries + write an event-id tombstone row. Tombstone timestamp = `max(existing.deleted_at, kind5.created_at)`. Re-insert of the deleted event id is suppressed by a `tombstones.contains(event_id)` check at insert time, returning `InsertOutcome::Tombstoned { id, kind5_event_id: Some(kind5.id), origin: Kind5 }`.
docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:153:  - For `a` tags (address format `<kind>:<pubkey>:<d-tag>`): if the target parameterized replaceable exists, same as `e` tag path. If it does **not** yet exist, write an address tombstone in `tombstones_addr` keyed by `(pubkey, kind, d-tag)`. When the target event is later inserted, the address tombstone match suppresses it and promotes an event-id tombstone for fast future lookups (see [`lmdb/keys.md`](lmdb/keys.md) §4.2).

54:+> **Audience:** kernel implementers landing M3 (persistence).
56:+> **Companion docs:** [`lmdb/trait.md`](lmdb/trait.md), [`lmdb/keys.md`](lmdb/keys.md), [`lmdb/gc.md`](lmdb/gc.md), [`lmdb/watermarks.md`](lmdb/watermarks.md), [`lmdb/tests.md`](lmdb/tests.md).

88:+- *Use `NostrLMDB` directly, no wrapper.* Loses every gap row above. Forces the kernel actor to know about LMDB transactions and a non-NMP concrete type, breaking the `Box<dyn EventStore>` substitutability M3 requires.
104:+    provenance.rs       — provenance sub-db (see lmdb/watermarks.md §2)
105:+    watermarks.rs       — watermark sub-db (see lmdb/watermarks.md §1)
120:+- **Watermarks / sync:** `read_watermark`, `write_watermark`, `list_watermarks_for_relay`.
138:+- `tombstones`: `target_id[32]` → `TombstoneRow { kind5_event_id, deleter_pubkey, deleted_at, sources: Vec<RelayUrl> }` (CBOR).
142:+All secondaries are maintained inside the same `RwTxn` as the primary write — atomicity is achieved by LMDB transactionality, not by post-hoc reconciliation.
146:+See [`lmdb/watermarks.md`](lmdb/watermarks.md) for full layout. Row shape (CBOR):
150:+  filter_hash: [u8; 32],     // BLAKE3 of canonicalised filter (see watermarks.md §3)
164:+See [`lmdb/watermarks.md`](lmdb/watermarks.md) §4. A `DomainModule` (per `kernel-substrate.md` §2) declares `const NAMESPACE: &'static str` and `const SCHEMA_VERSION: u32` plus `fn migrations() -> Vec<DomainMigration>`. The store assigns one LMDB sub-database per `(namespace, "data")`, plus one per `(namespace, index_name)` for each declared index. A `_meta` sub-database tracks `(namespace, current_version)`.
166:+The current `ModuleRegistry` (`crates/nmp-core/src/substrate/mod.rs:41`) discards the concrete `M: DomainModule` type after `register_domain::<M>()` returns — only the `ModuleDescriptor` is retained. The store cannot get from a namespace string back to `M::SCHEMA_VERSION` or `M::migrations()` at runtime. M3 adds a `DomainFactories { schema_version: fn() -> u32, migrations: fn() -> Vec<DomainMigration>, indexes: fn() -> Vec<DomainIndex> }` struct attached per descriptor, populated by capturing the `M::*` consts and fns in `fn`-pointer closures at register time. This matches the existing `key_fn: fn(&[u8]) -> Option<Vec<u8>>` pattern in `DomainIndex` (`crates/nmp-core/src/substrate/domain.rs:18`) — no `Box<dyn DomainModule>` and no new trait object-safety constraints on `DomainModule`. The change is additive to the substrate module surface. See [`lmdb/watermarks.md`](lmdb/watermarks.md) §4.1 for the registry-side code shape.
193:+ADR-0003's numbers are preserved as the M3 exit gate (§11 below): ≤ 100 MB working-set at 100 active views / 10k hot events / 1M cached on disk.
201:+- **Kind:5 self-delete.** Verify signature, scan referenced `e` and `a` tags, for each target `e_id` that is authored by the deleter or whose `a` address matches `(deleter_pubkey, kind, d-tag)`: delete the primary + all secondaries + write the tombstone row. Tombstone timestamp = `max(existing.deleted_at, kind5.created_at)`. Re-insert of the deleted event id is suppressed at insert time by a `tombstones.contains(event_id)` check.
223:+{"type":"tombstone","target_id":"abc...","kind5_event_id":"def...","deleter_pubkey":"...","deleted_at":1747000000,"sources":["wss://..."]}
224:+{"type":"watermark","filter_hash":"hex32","relay_url":"wss://...","synced_up_to":1747000000,"last_sync_method":"Negentropy","bytes_saved_vs_req":12345,"updated_at":1747000123}
230:+`nmp restore` is symmetric: read JSONL, replay through `insert()` for events (so all secondaries are rebuilt from scratch — provenance is restored separately by writing the sidecar row directly after each event), `write_watermark` for watermarks, `DomainHandle::put` for domain rows. Restore is idempotent: replaying the same dump twice produces the same store.
243:+| Kind:5 self-delete persists as tombstone | `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_kind5_tombstone.rs` |
244:+| Foreign kind:5 ignored | `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_kind5_foreign.rs` |
246:+| Watermarks survive restart, authoritative cache-miss | `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_watermarks.rs` |
265:+Each gate is measurable; any miss revises the design via an ADR before M3 is declared complete (per `plan.md` §1.6 "no silent endings").
269:+1. **`nostr-lmdb` LMDB environment sharing.** Can we open the same `lmdb::Environment` for both `NostrLMDB`'s sub-databases and our own NMP sub-databases (provenance, watermarks, claims, domain rows)? If yes, we get atomic cross-sub-db transactions for free (a single `RwTxn` covers event + provenance + secondary indexes). If `nostr-lmdb` insists on opening its own `Environment`, we lose that and the insert path needs a two-phase write with crash-recovery logic. Investigate before implementation — may require an upstream PR exposing `Environment` access.
270:+2. **Watermark `filter_hash` canonicalisation.** Two `Filter`s that are semantically identical but field-ordered differently must hash the same. The canonicalisation rule (likely: sort all tag-value arrays, sort kinds, sort authors, lexicographic field order before BLAKE3) needs to be specified once and shared with the planner so cache-coverage lookups hit. Candidate: a single `fn canonical_filter_hash(&Filter) -> [u8; 32]` in `nmp-core::store::watermarks`.
271:+3. **Projection cache durability.** Currently in-memory in the existing kernel (`kernel/mod.rs:293` `profiles: HashMap`). Do we persist projection caches as a `DomainModule` or rebuild from events at cold-start? Rebuild is simpler and avoids cache-staleness bugs but adds startup cost; persistence is faster but requires invalidation logic on kind:0 replacement. Recommended default: rebuild on cold-start, measure, decide whether to add the persistence layer in M3.x or M4.
273:+5. **iOS keychain-stored encryption-at-rest key for LMDB.** Out of scope for M3 (mentioned for M6 keychain work) but the schema must not assume cleartext-on-disk forever; reserve a `meta` row for `encryption_version: u32` so a future migration can wrap pages.
274:+6. **`ModuleRegistry::register_domain` API stability.** Adding `DomainFactories` to `ModuleDescriptor` is a non-breaking additive change to the public substrate API (existing callers using only the generic `register_domain::<M>()` continue to compile), but it commits us to keeping `DomainModule::SCHEMA_VERSION` and `DomainModule::migrations` as compile-time-resolvable items rather than object-safe methods. Confirm this with the substrate maintainer before M3 lands — if `DomainModule` is expected to support runtime composition (e.g., plugin loading), we need option (c): the actor passes the live `&[Box<dyn DomainModule>]` to `EventStore::open` instead. Recommended default: stay with `fn`-pointer factories; revisit if a plugin-loading use case appears.
285:+The M3 implementation deletes none of the existing files outright — the kernel's `events: HashMap` and `profiles: HashMap` are replaced by calls to `Box<dyn EventStore>` held inside the `Kernel` struct, and the per-field tests (`kernel/tests.rs`) shift to the new trait via `MemEventStore`. No public FFI surface changes.
434:+The relevant figure for the M3 exit gate is **working-set RSS at the configuration described in ADR-0003 §Decision**: 100 active views, 10k hot events, 1M cached on disk, ≤ 100 MB.
445:+| Watermarks (loaded as `HashMap` for hot lookups) | ~2 MB | M4 — assuming O(10k) watermarks (one per `(filter, relay)` pair) |
473:+    pub watermark_count: usize,
480:+Surfaced in the diagnostics screen alongside relay status (ADR-0007 §1). The Phase 1a.7 proof app already has the rendering scaffold (`ios/NmpStress/NmpStress/DiagnosticsView.swift`); M3 adds the StoreHealth row to it.
512:+| `watermarks` | NMP | `filter_hash[32] ‖ relay_url_bytes` | CBOR `WatermarkRow` | M4 NIP-77 sync state |
577:+    kind5_event_id: Option<[u8; 32]>,    // None for non-Kind5 origins
584:+Insert pre-check: before any new event hits the primary store, `tombstones.contains_key(event.id)` is consulted. A hit yields `InsertOutcome::Tombstoned { target_kind5_id }` and the event is dropped. This is the "later re-insertion is suppressed" behavior of §7.1.
590:+Key: `filter_hash[32] ‖ relay_url_bytes` — variable-length, exact-key lookups only. `filter_hash` is BLAKE3 of the canonical filter encoding (see `lmdb/watermarks.md` §3 for the canonicalisation algorithm).

1196:+# LMDB sub-design: watermarks, provenance, migrations
1198:+> Part of [`docs/design/lmdb-schema.md`](../lmdb-schema.md). Covers the three NMP-owned LMDB sub-databases that hold non-event durable state: `watermarks`, `provenance`, and the per-`DomainModule` sub-databases tracked by `_meta`.
1202:+Sub-db: `watermarks`. Populated by the M4 NIP-77 negentropy engine and consulted by the M2 subscription planner (per `docs/product-spec/subsystems.md` §7.2 "coverage-aware backfill").
1227:+pub fn coverage(&self, key: &WatermarkKey, now_s: u64) -> Coverage {
1228:+    match self.read_watermark(key) {
1230:+            Coverage::CompleteAsOf(row.synced_up_to),
1231:+        Ok(Some(row)) => Coverage::PartialUpTo(row.synced_up_to),
1232:+        Ok(None) => Coverage::Unknown,
1233:+        Err(_) => Coverage::Unknown,  // degraded; do not lie about completeness
1242:+On `LmdbEventStore::open()`, the store reads all `watermarks` rows and builds an in-memory `HashMap<WatermarkKey, WatermarkRow>` for hot lookups. Every `write_watermark` updates both the in-memory map and the LMDB row in a single `RwTxn`. Restart re-derives the map; we don't need a separate cache file.
1244:+For installations with O(100k+) watermarks (an edge case — typical apps see O(100)–O(10k)), the in-memory map switches to a lazy-loaded variant that pages on demand. Threshold and switching logic deferred to M4 when the negentropy engine's real-world row count is measured.
1290:+This produces a deterministic hash that is stable across `Filter` field-order variations and across Rust HashMap ordering randomness. The implementation lives at `crates/nmp-core/src/store/watermarks.rs::canonical_filter_hash(&Filter) -> [u8; 32]` and is the single source of truth for the planner + sync engine + dump format.
1292:+A filter with `limit: Some(N)` produces a *different* hash than the same filter without `limit` — because their cache-coverage semantics genuinely differ. A planner that wants to share a watermark across "limit=200" and "limit=500" requests of the same shape strips `limit` before hashing (this is a planner-side optimisation, not a store-side one).
1300:+The existing `ModuleRegistry` (`crates/nmp-core/src/substrate/mod.rs:36-79`) stores only `ModuleDescriptor { namespace, family, rust_type }` — the concrete `M: DomainModule` type is consumed by the generic `register_domain::<M>()` call and not retained, so the store has no runtime path from a namespace string back to `M::SCHEMA_VERSION` or `M::migrations()`. M3 extends `ModuleDescriptor` for the Domain family with two `fn`-pointer factories — matching the existing `DomainIndex::key_fn: fn(&[u8]) -> ...` pattern (`substrate/domain.rs:18`):
1303:+// Added in M3 — substrate/domain.rs
1370:+`kernel-substrate.md` §12 already flags "cross-module migration coordination" as an open question. M3 implements the per-module path; cross-module coordination is deferred to a future module that needs it. The trait surface does not preclude adding it later: a future `Vec<NamespaceDependency>` field on `DomainMigration` would let the runner topologically order modules' migrations.
1374:+The kernel's internal LMDB layout (provenance + secondaries + tombstones + watermarks) is itself versioned via the reserved `_kernel` namespace in `_meta`. Current version: `1`. A future schema change (e.g., a new secondary index) bumps this and runs a one-time rebuild from primary events.
1384:+- `StoreHealth.watermark_count` (per [`gc.md`](gc.md) §7) summarises the global count.
1386:+These are read-mostly paths; the only contention is between the actor's `write_watermark` calls (driven by M4 sync completions) and the diagnostics query, which is bounded by LMDB's MVCC reader semantics — no lock contention.

1401:docs/perf/firehose-bench/2026-05-17-comprehensive-findings.md:78:The reactivity model is directionally strong. Composite reverse indexes, per-view delta gates, batching, coalescing, and a hot/cold working-set split are the right defaults. The benchmark specifically supports the Applesauce/NDK-derived lesson that the UI should express interest declaratively while the core dedupes work and emits bounded deltas.
1402:docs/perf/firehose-bench/2026-05-17-comprehensive-findings.md:82:The memory figures are modeled as actor hot working set plus indexes and open views. Cold event bodies are treated as disk-resident. The allocation measurement uses a process-wide counting allocator and only samples the post-warmup hot path.

1905:docs/perf/codex-reviews/9fead0e.md:88:+- *Use `NostrLMDB` directly, no wrapper.* Loses every gap row above. Forces the kernel actor to know about LMDB transactions and a non-NMP concrete type, breaking the `Box<dyn EventStore>` substitutability M3 requires.
1916:docs/perf/codex-reviews/9fead0e.md:193:+ADR-0003's numbers are preserved as the M3 exit gate (§11 below): ≤ 100 MB working-set at 100 active views / 10k hot events / 1M cached on disk.
1919:docs/perf/codex-reviews/9fead0e.md:269:+1. **`nostr-lmdb` LMDB environment sharing.** Can we open the same `lmdb::Environment` for both `NostrLMDB`'s sub-databases and our own NMP sub-databases (provenance, watermarks, claims, domain rows)? If yes, we get atomic cross-sub-db transactions for free (a single `RwTxn` covers event + provenance + secondary indexes). If `nostr-lmdb` insists on opening its own `Environment`, we lose that and the insert path needs a two-phase write with crash-recovery logic. Investigate before implementation — may require an upstream PR exposing `Environment` access.
1920:docs/perf/codex-reviews/9fead0e.md:274:+6. **`ModuleRegistry::register_domain` API stability.** Adding `DomainFactories` to `ModuleDescriptor` is a non-breaking additive change to the public substrate API (existing callers using only the generic `register_domain::<M>()` continue to compile), but it commits us to keeping `DomainModule::SCHEMA_VERSION` and `DomainModule::migrations` as compile-time-resolvable items rather than object-safe methods. Confirm this with the substrate maintainer before M3 lands — if `DomainModule` is expected to support runtime composition (e.g., plugin loading), we need option (c): the actor passes the live `&[Box<dyn DomainModule>]` to `EventStore::open` instead. Recommended default: stay with `fn`-pointer factories; revisit if a plugin-loading use case appears.
1923:docs/perf/codex-reviews/9fead0e.md:285:+The M3 implementation deletes none of the existing files outright — the kernel's `events: HashMap` and `profiles: HashMap` are replaced by calls to `Box<dyn EventStore>` held inside the `Kernel` struct, and the per-field tests (`kernel/tests.rs`) shift to the new trait via `MemEventStore`. No public FFI surface changes.

2115:docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:47:On `LmdbEventStore::open()`, the store reads all `watermarks` rows and builds an in-memory `HashMap<WatermarkKey, WatermarkRow>` for hot lookups. Every `write_watermark` updates both the in-memory map and the LMDB row in a single `RwTxn`. Restart re-derives the map; we don't need a separate cache file.

2206:docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:1:# Design: LMDB schema + EventStore trait + GC policy (M3)
2215:docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:37:- *Use `NostrLMDB` directly, no wrapper.* Loses every gap row above. Forces the kernel actor to know about LMDB transactions and a non-NMP concrete type, breaking the `Box<dyn EventStore>` substitutability M3 requires.
2226:docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:142:ADR-0003's numbers are preserved as the M3 exit gate (§11 below): ≤ 100 MB working-set at 100 active views / 10k hot events / 1M cached on disk.
2229:docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:218:1. **`nostr-lmdb` LMDB environment sharing.** Can we open the same `lmdb::Environment` for both `NostrLMDB`'s sub-databases and our own NMP sub-databases (provenance, watermarks, claims, domain rows)? If yes, we get atomic cross-sub-db transactions for free (a single `RwTxn` covers event + provenance + secondary indexes). If `nostr-lmdb` insists on opening its own `Environment`, we lose that and the insert path needs a two-phase write with crash-recovery logic. Investigate before implementation — may require an upstream PR exposing `Environment` access.
2230:docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:223:6. **`ModuleRegistry::register_domain` API stability.** Adding `DomainFactories` to `ModuleDescriptor` is a non-breaking additive change to the public substrate API (existing callers using only the generic `register_domain::<M>()` continue to compile), but it commits us to keeping `DomainModule::SCHEMA_VERSION` and `DomainModule::migrations` as compile-time-resolvable items rather than object-safe methods. Confirm this with the substrate maintainer before M3 lands — if `DomainModule` is expected to support runtime composition (e.g., plugin loading), we need option (c): the actor passes the live `&[Box<dyn DomainModule>]` to `EventStore::open` instead. Recommended default: stay with `fn`-pointer factories; revisit if a plugin-loading use case appears.
2233:docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:234:The M3 implementation deletes none of the existing files outright — the kernel's `events: HashMap` and `profiles: HashMap` are replaced by calls to `Box<dyn EventStore>` held inside the `Kernel` struct, and the per-field tests (`kernel/tests.rs`) shift to the new trait via `MemEventStore`. No public FFI surface changes.

2303:    56	NIP-77 negentropy reconciliation is the default backfill mechanism. Every `(filter, relay)` pair the app touches is treated as a tracked sync target with a watermark. Live REQ remains the tailing path, but historical gaps consult coverage first and prefer sync over REQ scans when relays support it.
2469:   252	**Watermarks as a first-class type.** The engine reads and writes the `watermarks` table introduced in §7.1. A watermark answers two questions:
2479:   262	2. **View open.** When a view opens whose filter has a gap (per watermark/coverage), the engine reconciles the gap concurrently with the live REQ tail. Progress is visible in `SyncState`; the view payload streams in as events land.
2579:    31	**Sync watermarks.** The store maintains a per-`(filter_signature, relay_url)` table:
2582:    34	watermarks {
2600:    52	- Authoritative absence: only a complete coverage record/watermark can turn a miss into "not found." A non-empty cache result is not proof that a query is complete.
2611:    63	- **Coverage-aware backfill.** Before issuing historical traffic, the planner consults cache coverage/watermarks (§7.1). Complete coverage serves from cache; partial coverage schedules a gap fill; unknown coverage triggers bounded fetch/REQ or NIP-77 if supported. A non-empty cache result is never treated as complete by itself.
2649:   101	The gossip cache is the `nostr-gossip` crate; backend selection (in-memory vs SQLite) follows the storage backend choice. Watermarks (§7.1) intersect with outbox: a sync watermark is keyed by `(filter, relay)` and naturally tracks per-author per-relay coverage.

2873:    24	| Sync watermarks `(filter_hash, relay) → synced_up_to` | Out of scope; the crate does not know about logical filters or relay identity | `subsystems.md` §7.1 + §7.8; M4 NIP-77 engine needs them to be authoritative |
2880:    31	| `nmp dump` deterministic export | Out of scope | M3 exit criteria; M11 cross-app proof |
2886:    37	- *Use `NostrLMDB` directly, no wrapper.* Loses every gap row above. Forces the kernel actor to know about LMDB transactions and a non-NMP concrete type, breaking the `Box<dyn EventStore>` substitutability M3 requires.
2902:    53	    provenance.rs       — provenance sub-db (see lmdb/watermarks.md §2)
2903:    54	    watermarks.rs       — watermark sub-db (see lmdb/watermarks.md §1)
2918:    69	- **Watermarks / sync:** `read_watermark`, `write_watermark`, `list_watermarks_for_relay`.
2936:    87	- `tombstones`: `target_id[32]` → `TombstoneRow { kind5_event_id, deleter_pubkey, deleted_at, sources: Vec<RelayUrl> }` (CBOR).
2940:    91	All secondaries are maintained inside the same `RwTxn` as the primary write — atomicity is achieved by LMDB transactionality, not by post-hoc reconciliation.
2944:    95	See [`lmdb/watermarks.md`](lmdb/watermarks.md) for full layout. Row shape (CBOR):
2948:    99	  filter_hash: [u8; 32],     // BLAKE3 of canonicalised filter (see watermarks.md §3)
2962:   113	See [`lmdb/watermarks.md`](lmdb/watermarks.md) §4. A `DomainModule` (per `kernel-substrate.md` §2) declares `const NAMESPACE: &'static str` and `const SCHEMA_VERSION: u32` plus `fn migrations() -> Vec<DomainMigration>`. The store assigns one LMDB sub-database per `(namespace, "data")`, plus one per `(namespace, index_name)` for each declared index. A `_meta` sub-database tracks `(namespace, current_version)`.
2964:   115	The current `ModuleRegistry` (`crates/nmp-core/src/substrate/mod.rs:41`) discards the concrete `M: DomainModule` type after `register_domain::<M>()` returns — only the `ModuleDescriptor` is retained. The store cannot get from a namespace string back to `M::SCHEMA_VERSION` or `M::migrations()` at runtime. M3 adds a `DomainFactories { schema_version: fn() -> u32, migrations: fn() -> Vec<DomainMigration>, indexes: fn() -> Vec<DomainIndex> }` struct attached per descriptor, populated by capturing the `M::*` consts and fns in `fn`-pointer closures at register time. This matches the existing `key_fn: fn(&[u8]) -> Option<Vec<u8>>` pattern in `DomainIndex` (`crates/nmp-core/src/substrate/domain.rs:18`) — no `Box<dyn DomainModule>` and no new trait object-safety constraints on `DomainModule`. The change is additive to the substrate module surface. See [`lmdb/watermarks.md`](lmdb/watermarks.md) §4.1 for the registry-side code shape.
2991:   142	ADR-0003's numbers are preserved as the M3 exit gate (§11 below): ≤ 100 MB working-set at 100 active views / 10k hot events / 1M cached on disk.
2999:   150	- **Kind:5 self-delete.** Verify signature, scan referenced `e` and `a` tags, for each target `e_id` that is authored by the deleter or whose `a` address matches `(deleter_pubkey, kind, d-tag)`: delete the primary + all secondaries + write the tombstone row. Tombstone timestamp = `max(existing.deleted_at, kind5.created_at)`. Re-insert of the deleted event id is suppressed at insert time by a `tombstones.contains(event_id)` check.
3021:   172	{"type":"tombstone","target_id":"abc...","kind5_event_id":"def...","deleter_pubkey":"...","deleted_at":1747000000,"sources":["wss://..."]}
3022:   173	{"type":"watermark","filter_hash":"hex32","relay_url":"wss://...","synced_up_to":1747000000,"last_sync_method":"Negentropy","bytes_saved_vs_req":12345,"updated_at":1747000123}
3028:   179	`nmp restore` is symmetric: read JSONL, replay through `insert()` for events (so all secondaries are rebuilt from scratch — provenance is restored separately by writing the sidecar row directly after each event), `write_watermark` for watermarks, `DomainHandle::put` for domain rows. Restore is idempotent: replaying the same dump twice produces the same store.
3041:   192	| Kind:5 self-delete persists as tombstone | `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_kind5_tombstone.rs` |
3042:   193	| Foreign kind:5 ignored | `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_kind5_foreign.rs` |
3044:   195	| Watermarks survive restart, authoritative cache-miss | `crates/nmp-testing/tests/store_watermarks.rs` |
3063:   214	Each gate is measurable; any miss revises the design via an ADR before M3 is declared complete (per `plan.md` §1.6 "no silent endings").
3067:   218	1. **`nostr-lmdb` LMDB environment sharing.** Can we open the same `lmdb::Environment` for both `NostrLMDB`'s sub-databases and our own NMP sub-databases (provenance, watermarks, claims, domain rows)? If yes, we get atomic cross-sub-db transactions for free (a single `RwTxn` covers event + provenance + secondary indexes). If `nostr-lmdb` insists on opening its own `Environment`, we lose that and the insert path needs a two-phase write with crash-recovery logic. Investigate before implementation — may require an upstream PR exposing `Environment` access.
3068:   219	2. **Watermark `filter_hash` canonicalisation.** Two `Filter`s that are semantically identical but field-ordered differently must hash the same. The canonicalisation rule (likely: sort all tag-value arrays, sort kinds, sort authors, lexicographic field order before BLAKE3) needs to be specified once and shared with the planner so cache-coverage lookups hit. Candidate: a single `fn canonical_filter_hash(&Filter) -> [u8; 32]` in `nmp-core::store::watermarks`.
3069:   220	3. **Projection cache durability.** Currently in-memory in the existing kernel (`kernel/mod.rs:293` `profiles: HashMap`). Do we persist projection caches as a `DomainModule` or rebuild from events at cold-start? Rebuild is simpler and avoids cache-staleness bugs but adds startup cost; persistence is faster but requires invalidation logic on kind:0 replacement. Recommended default: rebuild on cold-start, measure, decide whether to add the persistence layer in M3.x or M4.
3071:   222	5. **iOS keychain-stored encryption-at-rest key for LMDB.** Out of scope for M3 (mentioned for M6 keychain work) but the schema must not assume cleartext-on-disk forever; reserve a `meta` row for `encryption_version: u32` so a future migration can wrap pages.
3072:   223	6. **`ModuleRegistry::register_domain` API stability.** Adding `DomainFactories` to `ModuleDescriptor` is a non-breaking additive change to the public substrate API (existing callers using only the generic `register_domain::<M>()` continue to compile), but it commits us to keeping `DomainModule::SCHEMA_VERSION` and `DomainModule::migrations` as compile-time-resolvable items rather than object-safe methods. Confirm this with the substrate maintainer before M3 lands — if `DomainModule` is expected to support runtime composition (e.g., plugin loading), we need option (c): the actor passes the live `&[Box<dyn DomainModule>]` to `EventStore::open` instead. Recommended default: stay with `fn`-pointer factories; revisit if a plugin-loading use case appears.
3083:   234	The M3 implementation deletes none of the existing files outright — the kernel's `events: HashMap` and `profiles: HashMap` are replaced by calls to `Box<dyn EventStore>` held inside the `Kernel` struct, and the per-field tests (`kernel/tests.rs`) shift to the new trait via `MemEventStore`. No public FFI surface changes.

3799:     1	# LMDB sub-design: watermarks, provenance, migrations
3801:     3	> Part of [`docs/design/lmdb-schema.md`](../lmdb-schema.md). Covers the three NMP-owned LMDB sub-databases that hold non-event durable state: `watermarks`, `provenance`, and the per-`DomainModule` sub-databases tracked by `_meta`.
3805:     7	Sub-db: `watermarks`. Populated by the M4 NIP-77 negentropy engine and consulted by the M2 subscription planner (per `docs/product-spec/subsystems.md` §7.2 "coverage-aware backfill").
3830:    32	pub fn coverage(&self, key: &WatermarkKey, now_s: u64) -> Coverage {
3831:    33	    match self.read_watermark(key) {
3833:    35	            Coverage::CompleteAsOf(row.synced_up_to),
3834:    36	        Ok(Some(row)) => Coverage::PartialUpTo(row.synced_up_to),
3835:    37	        Ok(None) => Coverage::Unknown,
3836:    38	        Err(_) => Coverage::Unknown,  // degraded; do not lie about completeness
3845:    47	On `LmdbEventStore::open()`, the store reads all `watermarks` rows and builds an in-memory `HashMap<WatermarkKey, WatermarkRow>` for hot lookups. Every `write_watermark` updates both the in-memory map and the LMDB row in a single `RwTxn`. Restart re-derives the map; we don't need a separate cache file.
3847:    49	For installations with O(100k+) watermarks (an edge case — typical apps see O(100)–O(10k)), the in-memory map switches to a lazy-loaded variant that pages on demand. Threshold and switching logic deferred to M4 when the negentropy engine's real-world row count is measured.
3893:    95	This produces a deterministic hash that is stable across `Filter` field-order variations and across Rust HashMap ordering randomness. The implementation lives at `crates/nmp-core/src/store/watermarks.rs::canonical_filter_hash(&Filter) -> [u8; 32]` and is the single source of truth for the planner + sync engine + dump format.
3895:    97	A filter with `limit: Some(N)` produces a *different* hash than the same filter without `limit` — because their cache-coverage semantics genuinely differ. A planner that wants to share a watermark across "limit=200" and "limit=500" requests of the same shape strips `limit` before hashing (this is a planner-side optimisation, not a store-side one).
3903:   105	The existing `ModuleRegistry` (`crates/nmp-core/src/substrate/mod.rs:36-79`) stores only `ModuleDescriptor { namespace, family, rust_type }` — the concrete `M: DomainModule` type is consumed by the generic `register_domain::<M>()` call and not retained, so the store has no runtime path from a namespace string back to `M::SCHEMA_VERSION` or `M::migrations()`. M3 extends `ModuleDescriptor` for the Domain family with two `fn`-pointer factories — matching the existing `DomainIndex::key_fn: fn(&[u8]) -> ...` pattern (`substrate/domain.rs:18`):
3906:   108	// Added in M3 — substrate/domain.rs
3973:   175	`kernel-substrate.md` §12 already flags "cross-module migration coordination" as an open question. M3 implements the per-module path; cross-module coordination is deferred to a future module that needs it. The trait surface does not preclude adding it later: a future `Vec<NamespaceDependency>` field on `DomainMigration` would let the runner topologically order modules' migrations.
3977:   179	The kernel's internal LMDB layout (provenance + secondaries + tombstones + watermarks) is itself versioned via the reserved `_kernel` namespace in `_meta`. Current version: `1`. A future schema change (e.g., a new secondary index) bumps this and runs a one-time rebuild from primary events.
3987:   189	- `StoreHealth.watermark_count` (per [`gc.md`](gc.md) §7) summarises the global count.
3989:   191	These are read-mostly paths; the only contention is between the actor's `write_watermark` calls (driven by M4 sync completions) and the diagnostics query, which is bounded by LMDB's MVCC reader semantics — no lock contention.

4388:**Findings**
4390:- High: [lmdb-schema.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:91) promises primary + secondary atomicity in one `RwTxn`, but [lmdb-schema.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:218) leaves shared `nostr-lmdb` environment access unresolved. Fix: make env/txn sharing a blocking ADR before M3 implementation, or specify crash-recovery/two-phase semantics.
4398:- High: [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:43) makes `Tombstoned` require `target_kind5_id: EventId`, but [keys.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/keys.md:85) allows NIP-40/Admin tombstones with no kind:5 id. Fix: use `kind5_event_id: Option<EventId>` plus `origin`, or return the tombstone row.
4402:- Medium: [lmdb-schema.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:67) names `scan_by_kind_dtag` and authoritative cache-coverage queries, but [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:162) only has `get_param_replaceable`, and [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:226) has no `coverage()` method. Fix: align the trait and docs; add `Coverage` to the trait if planner completeness depends on it.
4406:- Medium: [keys.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/keys.md:20) keys watermarks as `filter_hash || relay`, but [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:228) requires `list_watermarks_for_relay`. That scan is O(all watermarks). Fix: add a relay-first secondary or change the primary key order.
4408:- Medium: [watermarks.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:148) writes migration data, then [watermarks.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:150) writes `_meta` separately. Crash between them reruns a committed migration. Fix: commit migration writes and meta version in the same LMDB transaction; add crash/retry tests.
4410:- Medium: [tests.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:56) defers the “single insert path” enforcement test to v1.x. That is an M3 invariant. Fix: make it an M3 gate or remove the claim.

4427:- High: [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:43) makes `Tombstoned` require `target_kind5_id: EventId`, but [keys.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/keys.md:85) allows NIP-40/Admin tombstones with no kind:5 id. Fix: use `kind5_event_id: Option<EventId>` plus `origin`, or return the tombstone row.
4431:- Medium: [lmdb-schema.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:67) names `scan_by_kind_dtag` and authoritative cache-coverage queries, but [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:162) only has `get_param_replaceable`, and [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:226) has no `coverage()` method. Fix: align the trait and docs; add `Coverage` to the trait if planner completeness depends on it.
4435:- Medium: [keys.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/keys.md:20) keys watermarks as `filter_hash || relay`, but [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:228) requires `list_watermarks_for_relay`. That scan is O(all watermarks). Fix: add a relay-first secondary or change the primary key order.
4437:- Medium: [watermarks.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:148) writes migration data, then [watermarks.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:150) writes `_meta` separately. Crash between them reruns a committed migration. Fix: commit migration writes and meta version in the same LMDB transaction; add crash/retry tests.
4439:- Medium: [tests.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:56) defers the “single insert path” enforcement test to v1.x. That is an M3 invariant. Fix: make it an M3 gate or remove the claim.

codex
**Findings**

- High: [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:41) says `scan_by_kind_dtag` is newest-first, but [keys.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/keys.md:52) keys by `kind|pubkey|dtag`, with no timestamp. Same issue for all-kind `scan_by_kind_time` at [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:69) vs [keys.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/keys.md:68). Fix: add timestamp-ordered indexes, or change the trait contracts.

- Medium: [tests.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:56) claims `WriteCounting<S: EventStore>` can intercept primary sub-db writes, but an `EventStore` wrapper cannot see backend-internal LMDB `put()` calls. Fix: make this a backend test hook / write-layer instrumentation, not a pure trait wrapper.

- Medium: [gc.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/gc.md:62) counts `ids.len()` and [gc.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/gc.md:84) appends duplicates, but [gc.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/gc.md:184) says claim is idempotent. Fix: store per-claimer ids as a set or count only newly claimed ids.

- Medium: [lmdb-schema.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb-schema.md:75) cites doctrine D3 for “store errors do not cross FFI”; canonical doctrine is D6. Fix: change D3 to D6.

- Low: [watermarks.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/watermarks.md:32) shows `coverage(&WatermarkKey, now_s) -> Coverage`, while [trait.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/trait.md:117) exposes `coverage(&WatermarkKey) -> Result<Coverage, StoreError>`. Fix: align the signature and error behavior.

- Low: [tests.md](/Users/pablofernandez/Work/nostr-multi-platform/docs/design/lmdb/tests.md:1) is 322 LOC. No hard-ceiling breach, but it is over the 300 LOC soft limit.

**Verdict**

Not fully clean. ADR-0011 itself is well-grounded: real decision, consequences, fallback, alternatives. Most of the 12 fixes are present, but #6/#7/#8 and #11 are only partially addressed because the scan/test contracts still do not match the described implementation shape.

No `TODO`, `FIXME`, or `unimplemented` hits in the changed docs. No file exceeds 500 LOC.
